Villare Anglicum: OR A VIEW of the TOWNS OF ENGLAND.

Collected by the appointment of Sir HENRY SPELMAN Knight.

LONDON, Printed by R. Hodgkinsonne, dwelling in Thames Street near
Baynards-Castle, 1656.

To the Reader.
TRAVELING long Journeys is costly, at all times troublesome, at some times
dangerous: Yet is it both a general and generous desire of most men to be
acquainted with their native Country.

To satisfy them herein, this work is set forth; where thou may cross
Rivers without Boat or Bridge, climb up Mountains without pains, and go down
without danger: in a word thy eye may safely travel in a few hours over all
England, this Book presenting the Towns and Villages thereof, alphabetically
methodized, with the addition of their respective Counties, Hundreds, etc.

Now know this was collected by the appointment (at the charge, and for the
use) of that worthy Antiquarie Sir Henry Spelman, one of whom too much cannot
be said in his commendation; As who confuted that aspertion which is generally
cast on Antiquaries, that they are either supercilious or superstitious, either
proud or popishly affected, such his humble carriage to all persons and
sincecerity in the Protestant Religion.

Now it is enough to persuade others of the usefullnesse of this Treatise, that
so learned a man would cause it to be composed for his private perusal; and
because things of this nature the more public the more profitable, what
formerly was confined to his Study is now enlarged for the benefit of all who
please to make use thereof.

None can be so unreasonable as to expect that this Work should descend to the
specifying of the names of single Houses, it being impossibleto grind it so
small as to powder. What Dragg-Net is so capable, or can be so cast, to catch
all Minams that come under it? the performance therein will be satisfactory to
rational Readers if all considerable Villages be particularized.

Yet we believe the charitable Reader carries such a Chancery in his bosom as
to pardon some omissions, if casually some places have escaped observation.
Catalogues in this kind cannot be begun and finished at once, or by one Man,
(though never so industrious) but require a contribution of many well disposed
persons for the completing thereof.

And therefore if any shall be pleased to return to the Printer hereof the
names of such places as have slipped his notice, he shall have the hearty thanks
for, and the World the benefit by his instructions in the next Edition hereof.

It is also desired, that where faults are committed in false spelling of
names, such as dwell in the places (presumed the exactest Critics in their own
Orthographie) would be pleased to amend them and return their emendations, that
where the tongue of this Edition has lisped or faultered, it may speak plainer
and truer in the next, if it shall survive thereunto.

November 9. 1655. Thine R. H.
